It stated that although this and other loopholes were patched by TikTok before the end of March, the initial failure to correctly implement the restrictions, in addition to the effects from Kremlin's "fake news" laws, contributed to the formation of a "splInternet ... dominated by pro-war content" in Russia.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-239)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-guardian10mar2022-236) TikTok said that it had removed 204 accounts for swaying public opinion about the war while obscuring their origins and that its fact checkers had removed 41,191 videos for violating its misinformation policies.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-240)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-241)
In December 2023, [BBC News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_News "BBC News") reported that it had discovered nearly 800 fake TikTok accounts promoting Russian propaganda and disinformation. TikTok's own investigation found more than 12,000 fake accounts, including ones using additional languages such as English and Italian.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-242)
In September 2024, TikTok removed the accounts of Russian state media outlets [RT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RT_\(TV_network\) "RT \(TV network\)") and [Sputnik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputnik_\(news_agency\) "Sputnik \(news agency\)").[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-243)
### Feminism
The growth of popularity and access to TikTok has contributed to a growth in popularity of [digital feminist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Networked_feminism "Networked feminism") movements and discourse originating from the platform.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Sim%C3%B5es-2023-244)[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-245) Digital spaces like TikTok enable marginalized communities and activists, such as feminists, to feel safer and have an easier place to engage in discussion and dialogue or build an identity which might otherwise be impossible due to circumstances.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-246) The momentum of digital feminist movements through platforms like TikTok have additionally encouraged many social media agents and marketing campaigns around the world to adopt some degree of feminism as a part of their online image or personal brand.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-247) TikTok's unique platform organization, of spontaneous peer-peer information sharing, has enabled its utilization for community-engaged, digital knowledge mobilization and exchange between social justice communities.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-248) However inversely enabled by the platform's organic potential, both feminist challenges and anti-feminist reinforcement of dominant social, hierarchical, and gender values are widespread and instigated through TikTok, and content labeled as anti-feminist is itself popularized on TikTok.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Sim%C3%B5es-2023-244)
## Usage
### Demographics
See also: [List of most-followed TikTok accounts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_most-followed_TikTok_accounts "List of most-followed TikTok accounts")
TikTok tends to appeal to younger users, as 41% of its users are between the ages of 16 and 24. As of 2021, these individuals are considered [Generation Z](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generation_Z "Generation Z").[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Cervi_198%E2%80%93204-101) Among these TikTok users, 90% said they used the app daily.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-249) TikTok's geographical use in 2019 has shown that 43% of new users were from India before the social platform was banned in the country.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Mediakix-2019-250) But adults have also seen growth on TikTok. The share of US adults who regularly get news from TikTok hit 5% in 2025.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-251)
By July 2023, TikTok has become the primary news source for British teenagers on social media, with 28% of 12 to 15-year-olds relying on the platform, while traditional sources like [BBC One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_One "BBC One")/[Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Two "BBC Two") are more trusted at 82%, according to a report by UK regulator Ofcom.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-252) As of the first quarter of 2022, there were over 100 million monthly active users in the United States and 23 million in the UK. The average user, daily, was spending 1 hour and 25 minutes on the app and opening TikTok 17 times.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-wiredstats-253) Out of TikTok's top 100 male creators, a 2022 analysis reported 67% were white, with 54% having near-perfect [facial symmetry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facial_symmetry "Facial symmetry").[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-254)
#### Teenage mode
China heavily regulates how Douyin is used by minors in the country, especially after 2018.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Zhang-2023-255) Under government pressure, ByteDance introduced parental controls and a "teenage mode" that shows only whitelisted content, such as knowledge sharing, and bans pranks, superstition, dance clubs, and pro-LGBT content.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Hung-195) A mandatory screen time limit was put in place for users under the age of 14 and a requirement to link accounts to a real identity to prevent minors from lying about their age or using an adult's account. The differences between Douyin and TikTok have led some US politicians and commentators to accuse the company or the Chinese government of malicious intent.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Zhang-2023-255)[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-257) In March 2023, TikTok announced default screen time limits for users under the age of 18. Those under the age of 13 would need a passcode from their parents to extend their time.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Zhang-2023-255)
#### Underage users
As with other platforms popular with children, underage users may inadvertently reveal their daily routine and whereabouts, raising concerns of potential misuse by [sexual predators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_predator "Sexual predator").[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-2018-11-16-cnetfr-258)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-259) At the time of reporting (2018), TikTok had only two privacy settings, either private or completely public, without any middle ground.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-260) Comment sections of "sexy" videos, such as young girls dancing in revealing clothes, were found to contain requests for nude pictures. Despite safety concerns, TikTok began rolling out photo, video, and voice messaging around 2025.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-261) As of January 2026, the features are only available in certain regions, including the United States and Canada. In recent years, the US has charged and sentenced sexual predators for illegal activities on TikTok against underage girls.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-262)[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-263)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-264)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-265)
On 22 January 2021, the Italian Data Protection Authority demanded that TikTok temporarily suspend Italian users whose age could not be established.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-266) The order came after the death of a 10-year-old Sicilian girl involved in an Internet challenge. TikTok asked its users in Italy to confirm again that they were over 13 years old. By May, over 500,000 accounts had been removed for failing the age check.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-267)
In July 2021, the Dutch Data Protection Authority fined TikTok €750,000 for offering privacy statements only in English but not in Dutch. It noted that TikTok had implemented positive measures, such as forbidding direct messaging for users younger than 16 and allowing their parents to manage privacy settings directly through a paired family account, but the risk of children pretending to be older when creating their account remains.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-DutchEDPB-268)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-269) TikTok raised the minimum age for livestreaming from 16 to 18 after a BBC News investigation found hundreds of accounts going live from Syrian refugee camps. Thirty of them showed children begging for digital donation. TikTok reportedly made as much as a 70% commission on some of them, a figure that the company disputed.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-270)
In March 2024, the [Italian Competition Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Competition_Authority "Italian Competition Authority") fined TikTok €10 million for not protecting underage users adequately from harmful content such as the "French scar" challenge, which left heavy pinch marks on a person's cheeks.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-271) On December 30, 2024, Venezuela's Supreme Court fined TikTok $10 million over viral challenges that authorities say led to the deaths of three children. The court cited TikTok's negligence in failing to implement "necessary and adequate measures" to prevent the viral video challenges.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-272)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-273)
### Influencer marketing
The [BookTok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BookTok "BookTok") section at a [Barnes & Noble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barnes_%26_Noble "Barnes & Noble") store at [The Grove at Farmers Market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Grove_at_Farmers_Market "The Grove at Farmers Market") in Hollywood, February 2022
TikTok has provided a platform for users to create content not only for fun but also for money. As the platform has grown significantly over the past few years, it has allowed companies to advertise and rapidly reach their intended demographic through [influencer marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influencer_marketing "Influencer marketing").[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Dilon-2020-274) The platform's algorithm also contributes to the influencer marketing potential, as it picks out content according to the user's preference.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Haenlein-2020-275) Sponsored content is not as prevalent on the platform as it is on other social media apps, but brands and [influencers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influencers "Influencers") still can make as much as they would if not more in comparison to other platforms.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Haenlein-2020-275) Influencers on the platform who earn money through engagement, such as likes and comments, are referred to as "meme machines".[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Dilon-2020-274)
In 2021, _The New York Times_ reported that viral TikTok videos by young people relating the emotional impact of books on them, tagged with the label "[BookTok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BookTok "BookTok")", significantly drove sales of literature. Publishers were increasingly using the platform as a venue for influencer marketing.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-276)
In December 2022, NBC News reported in a television segment that some TikTok and YouTube influencers were being given free and discounted cosmetic surgeries in order for them to advertise the surgeries to users of the platforms.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-277) In 2022, it was reported that a trend called "de-influencing" had become popular on the platform as a backlash to influencer marketing. TikTok creators participating in this trend made videos criticizing products promoted by influencers and asked their audiences not to buy products they did not need. However, some creators participating in the trend started promoting alternative products to their audiences and earning commission from sales made through their [affiliate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affiliate_marketing "Affiliate marketing") links in the same manner as the influencers they were originally criticizing.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-278)[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-279)
In June 2022, reported that some of the influencers paid by _FeetFinder_ , a website that sells [foot fetish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foot_fetish "Foot fetish") content, did not disclose their videos were ads. FeetFinder said that it has suggested to influencers to be upfront about who was funding them. Existing sellers on FeetFinder said that the videos often misrepresented how "easy" it is to make money from posting feet pictures. Other TikTok creators have spoken out against accepting sponsorship deals indiscriminately and criticized those who posted undisclosed FeetFinder ads.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-280)
### Businesses
In October 2020, the e-commerce platform [Shopify](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shopify "Shopify") added TikTok to its portfolio of social media platforms, allowing online merchants to sell their products directly to consumers on TikTok.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-281) Some [small businesses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_business "Small business") have used TikTok to advertise and to reach an audience wider than the geographical region they would normally serve. The viral response to many small business TikTok videos has been attributed to TikTok's algorithm, which shows content that viewers at large are drawn to, but which they are unlikely to actively search for (such as videos on unconventional types of businesses, like [beekeeping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beekeeping "Beekeeping") and [logging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logging "Logging")).[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-282)
In 2020, digital media companies such as [Group Nine Media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_Nine_Media "Group Nine Media") and [Global](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Media_%26_Entertainment "Global Media & Entertainment") used TikTok increasingly, focusing on tactics such as brokering partnerships with TikTok influencers and developing branded content campaigns.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-283) Notable collaborations between larger brands and top TikTok influencers have included [Chipotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chipotle_Mexican_Grill "Chipotle Mexican Grill")'s partnership with [David Dobrik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Dobrik "David Dobrik") in May 2019[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-284) and [Dunkin' Donuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts "Dunkin' Donuts")' partnership with [Charli D'Amelio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charli_D%27Amelio "Charli D'Amelio") in September 2020.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-285)
### Sex workers
TikTok is regularly used by sex workers to promote pornographic content sold on platforms such as [OnlyFans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OnlyFans "OnlyFans").[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-286) One porn actor posted a viral song referring to himself as an "accountant", starting a trend.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-287) In 2020, TikTok updated their terms of service to ban content that promotes "premium sexual content", impacting a large number of adult content creators.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-288) In response, they began substituting words in their captions and videos and using filters to censor explicit images.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-289)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-290) Some adult content creators have found a way to game TikTok's recommendation algorithm by posting riddles, attracting a large number of viewers that struggled to solve them. This increased potential [Web traffic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_traffic "Web traffic") linked to the riddle posters' accounts on OnlyFans.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-291)
### Political
US president [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") references TikTok helped him win the [2024 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_election "2024 United States presidential election"), implications on [tariffs with China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_trade_war#2025 "China–United States trade war") and [restrictions in the US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restrictions_on_TikTok_in_the_United_States "Restrictions on TikTok in the United States"), March 2025.
The [Israeli Defense Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Force "Israeli Defense Force") (IDF) actively recruits [influencers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influencer "Influencer") on TikTok and other social media platforms, often with what commentators have dubbed "[Thirst traps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirst_trap "Thirst trap")".[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-292)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-293) In a separate case in 2021, the IDF awarded a TikToker who was one of its military police officers for promoting the image of Israel. She had more followers than IDF spokesperson [Ran Kochav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ran_Kochav "Ran Kochav") or Prime Minister [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-294)
Since 2021, TikTok has created "election centres" on its platform leading up to [European Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament") elections. About 30% of EP lawmakers use TikTok to get their messages across and to dispel misinformation.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-295)
In February 2024, the [re-election campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign "Joe Biden 2024 presidential campaign") for then-US president [Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") announced that it had opened a TikTok account while taking "advanced safety precautions". Biden posted his first video during [Super Bowl LVIII](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVIII "Super Bowl LVIII").[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-296) The move was criticized by a number of lawmakers over security concerns. Since 2022, the Biden administration had briefed TikTokers on news items such as the [Russo-Ukrainian war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_war_\(2022%E2%80%93present\) "Russo-Ukrainian war \(2022–present\)") and [student debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Student_debt "Student debt") relief in the United States.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-297)[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-298)
### Charities
Many charities use TikTok for fundraising and education, especially with younger audiences, charities using TikTok include; [Oregon Zoo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oregon_Zoo "Oregon Zoo"), [Shelter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shelter_\(charity\) "Shelter \(charity\)"), [Battersea Dogs and Cats Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battersea_Dogs_and_Cats_Home "Battersea Dogs and Cats Home"), [British Red Cross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Red_Cross "British Red Cross"), [American Heart Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Heart_Association "American Heart Association"), [United Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Way "United Way"), Catskill Animal Sanctuary and the [Black Country Living Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Country_Living_Museum "Black Country Living Museum").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-299)[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-300) Some TikTok influencers run their own events to raise money for charitable causes e.g. [Mercury Stardust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_Stardust "Mercury Stardust") runs the [TikTok-A-Thon for Trans Healthcare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok-A-Thon_for_Trans_Healthcare "TikTok-A-Thon for Trans Healthcare").[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-301)[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-302)[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-303) 'TikTok For Good' was created by TikTok to support fundraising on the platform.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-304)
[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-305) a live [workshop series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_class "Master class") in the [Indian states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_state "Indian state") of [Bihar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bihar "Bihar"), [Andhra Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh "Andhra Pradesh"), [Telangana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telangana "Telangana"), [Rajasthan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajasthan "Rajasthan"), [Jharkhand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jharkhand "Jharkhand") and [Jammu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu "Jammu") inspired by the hashtag #EduTok, in which video creators present factually for purposes of education. In 2022, TikTok banned fundraising for political accounts.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-306)
## Privacy and security concerns
[Privacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_privacy "Digital privacy") concerns have been brought up regarding the app.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Wong2019-307)[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-308) TikTok's privacy policy lists that the app collects usage information, [IP addresses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IP_address "IP address"), a user's [mobile carrier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobile_carrier "Mobile carrier"), [unique device identifiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organizationally_unique_identifier "Organizationally unique identifier"), [keystroke patterns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keystroke_dynamics "Keystroke dynamics"), and [location data](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Location_data "Location data"), among other data.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Mahadevan2020-309) Other information collected includes users inferred interests based on the content they view as well as content created by users.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Rodriguez-2021-28) TikTok is also able to track information about web users even if they are not users of the TikTok app. It collects information such as IP address, online browsing habits and web search history.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-310) TikTok can share data with its corporate group, including ByteDance. The company says that it employs access control and approval process overseen by a US-based team.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Rodriguez-2021-28) In June 2021, TikTok updated its privacy policy to include potential collection of [biometric data](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biometric_data "Biometric data"), including "faceprints and voiceprints", for special effects and other purposes. The terms said that user authorization would be requested if local law demands such.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-311) Experts considered them to be "vague" and their implications "problematic" for the United States due to the country's general lack of robust data privacy laws.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-312) In a November 2022 update to its European privacy policy, TikTok stated that its global corporate group employees from China and other countries could gain remote access to the user information of accounts from Europe based on "demonstrated need".[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-313)
A March 2021 study by the [Citizen Lab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citizen_Lab "Citizen Lab") found that TikTok did not collect data beyond the industry norms, what its policy stated, or without additional user permission.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-citizenlabexplained-198) In May 2023, _The Wall Street Journal_ reported that former employees complained about TikTok tracking users who had viewed LGBT-related content. The company said its algorithm tracks interests not identity, and non-LGBT users also view such content.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-314)
In March 2026, media and privacy regulators in Britain demanded for TikTok, along with other platforms to do more to keep children off their services, warning that companies were failing to enforce minimum age rules. As part of Britain's Online Safety Act, [Ofcom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ofcom "Ofcom") told TikTok to show by April 30 how they would tighten age checks and restrict strangers from connecting with children.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-315)
### Potential data collection by the Chinese government
Concerns have been raised about the potential control and influence of the Chinese government over TikTok's owner, ByteDance,[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Lee-2023-316) in particular the [extraterritorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterritorial_jurisdiction "Extraterritorial jurisdiction") implications of China's 2017 [National Intelligence Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Intelligence_Law "National Intelligence Law").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-317)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-318) An article in the law insists that all organizations and citizens shall "support, assist and cooperate with national intelligence efforts."[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-319)[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-320) Analysts differ in their assessments of the data collection risks. [Jim Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Andrew_Lewis "James Andrew Lewis") of the [Center for Strategic and International Studies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_for_Strategic_and_International_Studies "Center for Strategic and International Studies") said TikTok would have no right to appeal requests for data made by the Chinese government.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Rodriguez-2021-28) Some cybersecurity experts say individual users are not at risk.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-321) The United States has not offered any evidence of TikTok sharing such information with Chinese authorities.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-322) Keeping user data within the United States became the motivation behind TikTok's Project Texas.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Rodriguez-2021-28)
#### Access from China and United States response
In October 2021, following the [2021 Facebook leak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Facebook_leak "2021 Facebook leak") and controversies about social media ethics, a bipartisan group of United States lawmakers also pressed TikTok, YouTube, and Snapchat on questions of data privacy and moderation for age-appropriate content. Lawmakers also "hammered" TikTok about whether consumer data could be turned over to the Chinese government through ByteDance, its parent company in China.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-323) TikTok said it does not give information to China's government and "US user data" is stored within the country with backups in Singapore.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-324)
In June 2022, reported that leaked audio recordings of internal TikTok meetings reveal employees in China had access to overseas data, including a "master admin" who could see "everything". Some of the recordings were made during consultations with [Booz Allen Hamilton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Booz_Allen_Hamilton "Booz Allen Hamilton"), a US government contractor. A spokesperson of the contractor said some of the report's information was inaccurate but would neither confirm nor deny whether TikTok was one of its clients.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Baker-White-2022-325) As a consequence, the Senate Intelligence Committee including US lawmakers [Mark Warner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Warner "Mark Warner") and [Marco Rubio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Rubio "Marco Rubio") called for the [Federal Communications Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission "Federal Communications Commission") (FCC) to investigate ByteDance and whether TikTok had misled them.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-326)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-327) Following the reports, TikTok confirmed that employees in China could have access to US data.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-328) It also announced that US user traffic would now be routed through [Oracle Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_Cloud "Oracle Cloud") and that backup copies would be deleted from other servers.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-The_Verge-2022-329)
In June 2022, FCC Commissioner [Brendan Carr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brendan_Carr_\(lawyer\) "Brendan Carr \(lawyer\)") called for Google and Apple to remove TikTok from their app stores, saying sensitive data were being accessed from Beijing[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Brian-2022-330)[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Engadget-2022-331) and ByteDance would be "required by law to comply with [Chinese government] surveillance demands."[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Brian-2022-330) In November 2022, [Christopher A. Wray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_A._Wray "Christopher A. Wray"), director of the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation") (FBI), said the Chinese government could use TikTok for [influence operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influence_operations "Influence operations") on its users.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-332) In May 2023, a former ByteDance employee filed a wrongful termination lawsuit alleging that Hong Kong users' device information and communications, particularly those of demonstrators in the [2019–2020 Hong Kong protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Hong_Kong_protests "2019–2020 Hong Kong protests"), were accessed by [Chinese Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") members in 2018.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Associated_Press-2023-333)[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Wells-2023-334)[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-335) ByteDance denied the claims, saying the employee worked on a defunct project and that TikTok was pulled out of Hong Kong in 2020.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Wells-2023-334) The whistleblower claimed in a sworn court statement that his father in [mainland China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland_China "Mainland China") had been detained by the authorities in retaliation for his speaking to the media about alleged censorship by TikTok.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-336)
In June 2023, TikTok confirmed that some financial information, such as tax forms and [Social Security numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Security_number "Social Security number"), of American content creators are stored in China. This applies to those signing contracts with and receiving payment transactions from ByteDance. Whether similar information will remain exempt from being treated as "protected user data" is being negotiated with Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States (CFIUS).[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-337) A 2024 unclassified threat assessment by the [Director of National Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Director_of_National_Intelligence "Director of National Intelligence") said "TikTok accounts run by a [Chinese] propaganda arm reportedly targeted candidates" during the [2022 United States elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_United_States_elections "2022 United States elections").[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-338)
In April 2024, it was discovered that former employee Zen Goziker—allegedly the source of various leaks about TikTok to _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")_ , _Forbes_ , and —had made improbable claims. He has also spoken with law enforcement agencies and lawmakers hostile to TikTok. He has accused not only his former employer but also the [Attorney General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General "United States Attorney General"), the Director of National Intelligence, and the [Department of Homeland Security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security "Department of Homeland Security") for getting him fired.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-339)
### Project Texas
In response to security concerns of the United States government, TikTok has been working to silo privileged user data within the United States under oversight from the US government or a third party such as Oracle.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Fung-340) Named Project Texas, the initiative focuses on unauthorized access, state influence, and software security. A new subsidiary, TikTok US Data Security Inc. (USDS), was created to manage user data, software code, back-end systems, and content moderation. It would report to the Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States (CFIUS), not ByteDance or TikTok, even for hiring practices. Oracle would review and spot check the data flows through USDS. It would also digitally sign software code, approve updates, and oversee content moderation and recommendation. Physical locations would be established so that Oracle and the US government could conduct their own reviews.[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-lawfare-341) The company has been engaged in confidential negotiations over the project with CFIUS since 2021 and submitted its proposal but received little response from the panel afterward.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-342)
In March 2023, a former employee of the company said Project Texas did not go far enough and that a complete "re-engineering" would be needed. TikTok responded by saying that Project Texas already is a re-engineering of the app and that the former employee left in 2022 before the project specifications were finalized.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-gizmodo.com-343) Other former employees had their own takes on the situation. A data scientist said US user data were emailed to ByteDance workers in China to identify viewer interests. A manager recounted that there was a lot more separation on the technical side between TikTok and ByteDance by the time he left. Another said TikTok had to employ better data collection practices than [Meta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta_Platforms "Meta Platforms") or [Google](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google "Google") due to the scrutiny it received.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Sternlicht-2024-26)
On 22 January 2026, US President [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") and TikTok announced that the company had joined a joint venture, which will run as an independent entity while operating under defined safeguards that protect national security for US users. Adam Presser who was previously TikTok's head of operations and trust and safety will serve as CEO, while TikTok's current CEO Shou Chew will be a director of the new venture.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-344)
The new investors are loyal to Trump.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-The_Independent-345) TikTok has subsequently been accused of censoring content critical of Trump and his administration.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-The_Independent-345) The censorship includes censoring words such as "[Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein "Jeffrey Epstein")" and videos that criticize Trump or [Immigration and Customs Enforcement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement "Immigration and Customs Enforcement") (ICE).[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-The_Independent-345) The resulting backlash saw TikTok competitor [UpScrolled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UpScrolled "UpScrolled") receive record downloads and rise to second in the Apple's App Store rankings.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-The_Independent-345)[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-346)[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-347)
### Project Clover
TikTok has faced criticism for transferring European user data to servers in the United States. It is holding discussions with UK's [National Cyber Security Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Cyber_Security_Centre_\(United_Kingdom\) "National Cyber Security Centre \(United Kingdom\)") about a "Project Clover" for storing European information locally. The company plans to build two data centers in Ireland and one more in Norway. A third party will oversee the cybersecurity policies, data flows, and personnel access independently of TikTok.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-348)[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-349)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Goujard2023-21)
### Journalist spying scandal
In October 2022, _Forbes_ reported that a team at ByteDance planned to surveil certain US citizens for undisclosed reasons. TikTok said that the tracking method suggested by the report would not be feasible because precise GPS information is not collected by the platform.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-350)[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-351) In December 2022, ByteDance confirmed after internal investigation that the data of two journalists and their close contacts had been accessed by its employees from China and the United States. It was intended to uncover sources of leaks who might have met with the journalists from _Forbes_ and the _Financial Times_. The data included IP addresses, which can be used to approximate a user's location. ByteDance stated that it fired four employees in response.[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-352)
The incident is being investigated by the US Department of Justice and FBI.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-353)[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-354)[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Fung-340) The US Attorney for the [Eastern District of Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_District_of_Virginia "Eastern District of Virginia") reportedly subpoenaed information from ByteDance regarding its surveillance of journalists on TikTok.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Baker-White-2023-355) In December 2023, the [United States House Select Committee on Strategic Competition between the United States and the Chinese Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_Strategic_Competition_between_the_United_States_and_the_Chinese_Communist_Party "United States House Select Committee on Strategic Competition between the United States and the Chinese Communist Party") inquired the FBI about the status of the case.[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-356)
### Software code
In January 2020, [Check Point Research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Check_Point "Check Point") discovered a [vulnerability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulnerability_\(computing\) "Vulnerability \(computing\)") through which a [hacker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_hat_\(computer_security\) "Black hat \(computer security\)") could [spoof](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spoofing_attack "Spoofing attack") TikTok's official [SMS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SMS "SMS") messages and replace them with malicious links to gain access to user accounts. It was later [patched](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patch_\(computing\) "Patch \(computing\)") by TikTok.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-357) In August 2020, _The Wall Street Journal_ reported that TikTok tracked Android user data, including [MAC addresses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MAC_address "MAC address") and [IMEIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMEI "IMEI"), with a tactic in violation of Google's policies.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-358)[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-359)
In August 2022, software engineer and security researcher Felix Krause found that in-app browsers from TikTok and other platforms contained [codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program "Computer program") for [keylogger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keylogger "Keylogger") functionality but did not have the means to further investigate whether any data was tracked or recorded. TikTok said that the code is disabled.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-360)
### Regulatory actions
#### US Federal Trade Commission
On 27 February 2019, the United States [Federal Trade Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission "Federal Trade Commission") (FTC) reached a [consent decree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consent_decree "Consent decree") with ByteDance, fining it US$5.7 million for collecting information from minors under the age of 13 in violation of the [Children's Online Privacy Protection Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Children%27s_Online_Privacy_Protection_Act "Children's Online Privacy Protection Act") (COPPA).[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-361) ByteDance responded by adding a kids-only mode to TikTok which blocks the upload of videos, the building of user profiles, direct messaging, and commenting on others' videos, while still allowing the viewing and recording of content.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-362) In May 2020, an advocacy group filed a complaint with the FTC saying that TikTok had violated the terms of the February 2019 consent decree with the FTC, which sparked subsequent congressional calls for a renewed FTC investigation.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-363)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-364)[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-365) In March 2022, following a [class action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_action "Class action") lawsuit for violations of COPPA, TikTok settled for US$1.1 million.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-366)[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-367) In March 2024, it was reported that the FTC continues to investigate TikTok.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-368) In August 2024, the FTC and US Department of Justice filed a joint lawsuit alleging violations of the 2019 consent decree.[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-369)
In September 2021, the Ireland [Data Protection Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_Protection_Commission "Data Protection Commission") (DPC) launched investigations into TikTok concerning the protection of minors' data and transfers of personal data to China.[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-370)[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-371) The Irish DPC became the lead agency to handle such matters after TikTok established an office in the country, taking over investigations started by Dutch and Italian authorities.[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-372)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-DutchEDPB-268) In September 2023, the DPC fined TikTok €345 million for violations of the [General Data Protection Regulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Data_Protection_Regulation "General Data Protection Regulation") (GDPR) vis-à-vis the mishandling of children data.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-373)[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-374) In April 2025, the Ireland DPC fined TikTok over €500 million for illegally sending European user data to China.[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-375)[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-376) In July 2025, the DPC opened a new investigation into TikTok for unauthorized transfers of user data to China.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-377)
In February 2019, the United Kingdom's [Information Commissioner's Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Commissioner%27s_Office "Information Commissioner's Office") (ICO) launched an investigation of TikTok following the fine ByteDance received from the United States Federal Trade Commission (FTC). Speaking to a parliamentary committee, Information Commissioner [Elizabeth Denham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Denham "Elizabeth Denham") said that the investigation focuses on the issues of private data collection, the kind of videos collected and shared by children online, as well as the platform's open messaging system which allows any adult to message any child. She noted that the company was potentially violating the GDPR which requires the company to provide different services and different protections for children.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-378) In April 2023, the ICO imposed a £12.7 million fine on TikTok for misusing children's data.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-379)[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-380) In March 2025, the ICO opened another investigation into TikTok concerning its use of children's personal information to recommend content to them.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-381)
### Pending investigations
#### Texas
In February 2022, [Texas Attorney General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_Attorney_General "Texas Attorney General") [Ken Paxton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Paxton "Ken Paxton") initiated an investigation into TikTok for alleged violations of children's privacy and facilitation of [human trafficking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_trafficking "Human trafficking").[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-382)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-383) Paxton claimed that the [Texas Department of Public Safety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_Department_of_Public_Safety "Texas Department of Public Safety") gathered several pieces of content showing the attempted recruitment of teenagers to smuggle people or goods across the [Mexico–United States border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border "Mexico–United States border"). He claimed the evidence may prove the company's involvement in "human smuggling, sex trafficking and drug trafficking". The company claimed that no illegal activity of any kind is supported on the platform.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-384)
#### Turkey
In 2022, Turkey's [Financial Crimes Investigation Board](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Crimes_Investigation_Board_\(Turkey\) "Financial Crimes Investigation Board \(Turkey\)") (MASAK) initiated a probe into TikTok in relation to millions of dollars in fund transfers involving TikTok accounts that were suspected of [money laundering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Money_laundering "Money laundering") or [terrorism financing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_financing "Terrorism financing").[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Michael-2024-385)
#### Privacy Commissioner of Canada
In February 2023, the [Privacy Commissioner of Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privacy_Commissioner_of_Canada "Privacy Commissioner of Canada"), along with its counterparts in Alberta, British Columbia, and Quebec, launched an investigation into TikTok's data collection practices.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-386) In 2025, a Canadian investigation found that TikTok had collected sensitive personal data from children in violation of federal privacy laws.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-387)
#### European Commission
In February 2024, the [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") launched an investigation into TikTok for potential violations of the [Digital Services Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_Services_Act "Digital Services Act") (DSA), involving content aiming at children and advertising transparency.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-388) In April 2024, the European Commission opened a second investigation into TikTok to assess whether it broke EU law.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-389) In October 2024, the European Commission requested additional information from TikTok relating to its algorithm and risks around elections, mental health, and protection of minors.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-390) In December 2024, the European Commission announced an investigation into TikTok over [accusations of Russian interference in the 2024 Romanian presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accusations_of_Russian_interference_in_the_2024_Romanian_presidential_election "Accusations of Russian interference in the 2024 Romanian presidential election").[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-391) In May 2025, the European Commission found TikTok had violated digital advertising rules under the DSA.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-392)
#### Australian Information Commissioner inquiry
In December 2023, the [Office of the Australian Information Commissioner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_the_Australian_Information_Commissioner "Office of the Australian Information Commissioner") announced an inquiry into TikTok's data harvesting of Australian citizens amid allegations that it contravened Australian privacy law.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-393)
## Controversies
Further information: [Lawsuits involving TikTok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawsuits_involving_TikTok "Lawsuits involving TikTok")
### Cyberbullying
Further information: [Problematic social media use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problematic_social_media_use "Problematic social media use")
noted in 2018 that bullies and trolls were relatively rare on TikTok compared to other platforms.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-theweek-394) Nonetheless, several users have reported [cyberbullying](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyberbullying "Cyberbullying") via features such as Duet or React, which is used to interact with followers.[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-395) A trend making fun of [autism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autism "Autism") eventually created a huge backlash, even on the platform itself, and the company ended up removing the hashtag altogether.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-396)[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-397) Parents filming how their children reacted to people with disability, often in terror, led to criticisms of [ableism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ableism "Ableism").[] In December 2019, following a report by German digital rights group [netzpolitik.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netzpolitik.org "Netzpolitik.org"), TikTok admitted that it had suppressed videos by disabled users as well as LGBTQ+ users in a purported temporary effort to limit cyberbullying.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-398)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-theintercept-192) _[TikTok: Murder Gone Viral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok:_Murder_Gone_Viral "TikTok: Murder Gone Viral")_ , a documentary series produced by [ITV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITV_\(TV_network\) "ITV \(TV network\)"), highlights how cyberbullying and TikTok's role as a social media platform has led to the murder of certain individuals.[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-399)
### Addiction and mental health
Further information: [Digital media use and mental health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_media_use_and_mental_health "Digital media use and mental health") and [Social media and suicide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_media_and_suicide "Social media and suicide")
There are concerns that some users may find it hard to stop using TikTok.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-scmp-400) Internal TikTok research has documented the addiction potential of the app.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-401) In April 2018, an addiction-reduction feature was added to Douyin.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-scmp-400) This encouraged users to take a break every 90 minutes.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-scmp-400) Later in 2018, the feature was rolled out to the TikTok app. TikTok uses popular [influencers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influencers "Influencers") to encourage viewers to stop using the app and take a break.[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-402)
Many were also concerned with the app affecting users' [attention spans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attention_span "Attention span") due to the short-form nature of the content. This is a concern as many of TikTok's audience are younger children, whose brains are still developing.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-403) TikTok executives and representatives have noted and made aware to advertisers on the platform that users have poor attention spans. The company's survey reported that nearly 50% of social media users find it stressful to watch a video longer than a minute and a third of users watch videos at double speed. Their short attention spans posed a challenge for TikTok to pivot towards longer content formats.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-wiredstats-253) TikTok has also received criticism for enabling children to purchase coins which they can send to other users.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-404)
Daily hours of entertainment screen media (Social Medias) may displace healthy behaviors such as socializing face to face, chores, hobbies, homework, family meals time, exercise, and sufficient sleep. Insomnia is considered a strong mediator between screen media time and mental health symptoms which implies that engaging in screen time pushes out adequate sleep and leads to decreased mental health.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-405)
In February 2022, _The Wall Street Journal_ reported that "[Mental-health professionals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_health_professional "Mental health professional") around the country are growing increasingly concerned about the effects on teen girls of posting sexualized TikTok videos."[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-406) In March 2022, a coalition of US state attorneys general launched an investigation into TikTok's effect on children's mental health.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-407) In June 2022, TikTok introduced the ability to set a maximum uninterrupted screen time allowance, after which the app blocks off the ability to navigate the feed. The block only lifts after the app is exited and left unused for a set period of time. Additionally, the app features a dashboard with statistics on how often the app is opened, how much time is spent browsing it and when the browsing occurs.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-408)
Since 2021, it has been reported that accounts engaging with contents related to suicide, self-harm, or eating disorders were shown more similar videos. Some users were able to circumvent TikTok filters by writing in code or using unconventional spelling. The company has faced multiple lawsuits pertaining to wrongful deaths. TikTok said it is working to break up these "rabbit holes" of similar recommendations. US searches for eating disorder receive a prompt that offers mental health resources.[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-409)[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-410)[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-411)
In 2021, the platform revealed that it will be introducing a feature that will prevent teenagers from receiving notifications past their bedtime. The company will no longer send push notifications after 9 pm to users aged between 13 and 15. For 16 to 17 year olds, notifications will not be sent after 10 pm.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-412) In March 2023, TikTok announced default screen time limits for users under the age of 18.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-413) _The Wall Street Journal_ has reported that doctors experienced a surge in reported cases of [tics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tics "Tics"), tied to an increasing number of TikTok videos from content creators with [Tourette syndrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tourette_syndrome "Tourette syndrome"). Doctors suggested that the cause may be a social one as users who consumed content showcasing various tics would sometimes develop tics of their own,[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-414) akin to [mass psychogenic illness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_psychogenic_illness "Mass psychogenic illness").[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Olvera_Stebbins_Goetz_Kompoliti_2021_pp._1200%E2%80%931205-415)[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-M%C3%BCller-Vahl_Pisarenko_Jakubovski_Fremer_2021_pp._476%E2%80%93480-416)
In May 2024, [Nebraska Attorney General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebraska_Attorney_General "Nebraska Attorney General") [Mike Hilgers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Hilgers "Mike Hilgers") filed a lawsuit against TikTok for allegedly harming minors' mental health through an algorithm designed to be cultivate compulsive behavior.[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-417) In October 2024, US senators [Richard Blumenthal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Blumenthal "Richard Blumenthal") and [Marsha Blackburn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marsha_Blackburn "Marsha Blackburn") requested that TikTok turn over "all documents and information" related to child safety disclosures that were uncovered by [NPR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NPR "NPR") and [Kentucky Public Radio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kentucky_Public_Radio "Kentucky Public Radio").[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-418)
As of March 2025, strong scientific understanding of TikTok's effects on user's mental health "remains elusive". A 2025 [meta-analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta-analysis "Meta-analysis") found that use of TikTok was [correlated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Correlation "Correlation") with symptoms of [anxiety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anxiety "Anxiety") and [depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_\(mood\) "Depression \(mood\)"), with stronger links in females and users under 24 years old.[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-419) In November 2025, French prosecutors opened a probe into TikTok, citing concerns that its algorithms could push vulnerable young people to suicide.[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-420)
The [Ministry of Education (Taiwan)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_\(Taiwan\) "Ministry of Education \(Taiwan\)") has warned against the harmful impact of TikTok and related app RedNote on [body image](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_image "Body image") and ensuing [self harm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self_harm "Self harm") related to [weight loss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weight_loss "Weight loss") especially in teenagers. Civil society groups warn that these apps push users down "rabbit holes" and then surround them in an "information cocoon".[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-421)
### 2022 medication shortage
In November 2022, Australia's medical regulatory agency, the [Therapeutic Goods Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Therapeutic_Goods_Administration "Therapeutic Goods Administration") (TGA) reported that there was a global shortage of the diabetes medication Ozempic. According to the TGA, the rise in demand was caused by an increase in [off-label](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Off-label "Off-label") prescription of the drug for weight loss purposes.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-422) In December 2022, with the United States experiencing a shortage as well, it was reported that the huge increase in demand for the medicine was caused by a weight loss trend on TikTok, where videos about the drug exceeded 360 million views.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-423)[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-424)[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-425) [Wegovy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wegovy "Wegovy"), a drug that has been specifically approved for treating obesity, also became popular on the platform after [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk "Elon Musk") credited it for helping him lose weight.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-426)[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-427)
### Workplace conditions
See also: [Overwork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overwork "Overwork")
Several former employees of the company have claimed of poor workplace conditions, including the start of the workweek on Sunday to cooperate with [Chinese time zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTC%2B08:00 "UTC+08:00") and excessive workload. Employees claimed they averaged 85 hours of meetings per week and would frequently [stay up all night](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_deprivation "Sleep deprivation") in order to complete tasks. Some employees claimed the workplace's schedule operated similarly to the [996 schedule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/996_schedule "996 schedule"). The company has a stated policy of working from 10 AM to 7 PM five days per week (63 hours per week), but employees noted that it was encouraged for employees to work after hours. One female worker complained that the company did not allow her adequate time to change her [feminine hygiene product](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menstrual_hygiene_management "Menstrual hygiene management") because of back-to-back meetings. Another employee noted that working at the company caused her to seek [marriage therapy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage_therapy "Marriage therapy") and lose an unhealthy amount of weight.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-428) In response to the allegations, the company noted that they were committed to allowing employees "support and flexibility".[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-429)[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-430)
In September 2023, two former ByteDance employees filed a formal complaint with the [US Equal Employment Opportunity Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Equal_Employment_Opportunity_Commission "US Equal Employment Opportunity Commission") (EEOC) asking the EEOC to investigate TikTok's practice of retaliation against workers who complain about [discrimination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrimination "Discrimination").[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-431)
Further information: [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict") and [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war")
With reports that Palestinians resorted to TikTok for promoting their cause after platforms like Facebook and [Twitter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter "Twitter") blocked their content,[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-432) Israeli analyst [Yoni Ben-Menachem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoni_Ben-Menachem "Yoni Ben-Menachem") called the app a "tool of dangerous influence" inciting violence against Israelis.[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-433)[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-434) According to [Ynet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ynet "Ynet"), the Palestinian militant group [Lion's Den](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lions%27_Den_\(militant_group\) "Lions' Den \(militant group\)") gained much of their popularity through TikTok.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-435) In February 2023, [Otzma Yehudit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otzma_Yehudit "Otzma Yehudit") politician [Almog Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almog_Cohen_\(politician\) "Almog Cohen \(politician\)") advocated blocking TikTok for all of [East Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem").[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-436) US lawmakers [wanting to ban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H.R._7521 "H.R. 7521") TikTok accused the platform of pushing pro-[Hamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") and pro-Palestine content.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Roscoe-437)[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Jennings-438)
According to _[The Times of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times_of_Israel "The Times of Israel")_ , [antisemitism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism "Antisemitism") at the company was "rampant" after the [October 7 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_7_attacks "October 7 attacks"), allowing anti-Jewish and anti-Israel content to increase on the platform.[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-439) Prominent Jewish individuals such as [Sacha Baron Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen "Sacha Baron Cohen"), [Debra Messing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debra_Messing "Debra Messing"), [Amy Schumer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amy_Schumer "Amy Schumer"), and TikTok creator [Miriam Ezagui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miriam_Ezagui "Miriam Ezagui") raised the issue with Adam Presser, TikTok's head of operations, and Seth Melnick, its global head of user operations, both also Jewish.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-440)
TikTok said that a significant proportion of its userbase comes from non-US regions such as the [Middle East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East") and [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia") and that hashtags should not be [cherry-picked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cherry_picking "Cherry picking") due to differences in the number of views per post and the age of a post or tag. The popularity of pro-Palestine content has also been explained by the app's younger user base, which has shifted its sympathy away from [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") towards the [Palestinians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinians "Palestinians").[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Roscoe-437)[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Jennings-438)
The [Jewish Federations of North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Federations_of_North_America "Jewish Federations of North America") expressed support for TikTok to be banned, while Israel's critics denounced the "criminalisation of pro-Palestinian voices", including on TikTok, which has been used to condemn "Israel's [atrocities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombing_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Bombing of the Gaza Strip")", according to .[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-441) TikTok was also accused by Malaysia's minister of communications, [Fahmi Fadzil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahmi_Fadzil "Fahmi Fadzil") of suppressing pro-Palestinian content. The company stated it banned praising Hamas and removed more than 775,000 videos and 14,000 livestreams.[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-442)[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-443)
There has also been reporting on the trend of [Israeli soldiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IDF "IDF") using TikTok to mock Palestinians and boast about their actions in the Gaza Strip.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-NYTtoler-444)[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-445)[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Buxbaum-446)[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-447) According to Huda Abudagga, a legal advisor for the British nonprofit Law for Palestine, many of the videos show soldiers partaking in actions, such as the destruction of Palestinian homes as well as the theft of private and public property, that are considered [war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crimes "War crimes") under international law.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Buxbaum-446) Similarly, four legal experts consulted by the _New York Times_ said that the videos "could be used to show unlawful destruction, a violation of the [Geneva Conventions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Conventions "Geneva Conventions")."[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-NYTtoler-444) One such video, which showed Israeli soldiers dancing and singing "There are no uninvolved civilians", was included as evidence of genocidal intent in [South Africa's case against Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa%27s_genocide_case_against_Israel "South Africa's genocide case against Israel") before the [International Court of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice "International Court of Justice").[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Buxbaum-446)
In November 2023, Osama bin Laden's 2002 "[Letter to the American people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_to_the_American_people "Letter to the American people")" went viral on TikTok and other social media. In the letter, he denounced the US and its support for Israel, and supported [al-Qaeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda")'s war against the US as a defensive struggle. Numerous social media users, including Americans, expressed their opposition to US foreign policy by sharing the resurfaced copies of the letter and its contents. _The Guardian_ website removed the letter after displaying it for more than 20 years, and TikTok began issuing takedowns of videos featuring the letter.[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-448) Reporting in _The Washington Post_ suggested that the virality of the letter had been limited prior to media coverage, having never trended on TikTok. Many of the TikTok videos covering the letter were critical of bin Laden, and media coverage had exaggerated its significance while elevating the virality of the letter.[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-449)
In July 2025, TikTok hired [Erica Mindel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erica_Mindel "Erica Mindel"), a former [Israel Defense Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces") instructor and contractor for the US State Department's Special Envoy to Monitor and Combat Antisemitism, as its Public Policy Manager of Hate Speech.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-450)[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-451)
Starting in 2026, TikTok began cracking down on the accounts of Palestinian activists and journalists, including [Bisan Owda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bisan_Owda "Bisan Owda"), who had reported on the human rights abuses taking place in Gaza. Media outlets such as Al Jazeera verified that TikTok's new algorithm hid content depending on the user's region, with the app hiding Palestinian content from users in the Middle East.[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-452)
### Child exploitation in Kenya
An investigation in 2025 found that TikTok was profiting from sexual livestreams in [Kenya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenya "Kenya") involving minors, with teenagers as young as 15 using the platform to solicit explicit content. Women in Kenya reported earning money through TikTok Lives, where coded [sexual slang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_slang "Sexual slang") and emoji gifts facilitated transactions, with explicit content often delivered via other platforms. TikTok takes a 70% cut of these livestream earnings and has been aware of [child exploitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse "Child sexual abuse") since at least 2022. Many moderators say the company's content policies are ineffective, and [digital pimps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procuring_\(prostitution\) "Procuring \(prostitution\)") exploit underage users on the large. Kenya lacks adequate moderation, and TikTok denies any sort of wrongdoing.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-453)
In response to the exposé, [Kenya's Communications Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communications_Authority_of_Kenya "Communications Authority of Kenya") (CA) launched a formal inquiry, directing TikTok to remove all [sexual content](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_content "Sexual content") involving minors and submit a detailed plan to strengthen its moderation and child protection systems.[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-454)[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-455)[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-456)
### Lobbying by competitors
According to _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")_ , [Meta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta_Platforms "Meta Platforms") hired the [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_\(United_States\) "Republican Party \(United States\)") consulting firm [Targeted Victory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Targeted_Victory "Targeted Victory") to run a campaign aimed at turning public opinion against TikTok. Internal emails revealed that the firm sought to portray TikTok as "the real threat" and encouraged headlines such as "From dances to danger: how TikTok has become the most harmful social media space for kids." Operatives promoted stories to local media that tied TikTok to allegedly dangerous trends among teenagers, including the 2021 "[devious lick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devious_lick "Devious lick")" vandalism challenge, which evidence shows originated on Facebook. The campaign also sought to deflect attention from criticisms of Meta's own privacy and antitrust issues. A Meta spokesperson defended the effort, saying that all platforms, including TikTok, should face equal scrutiny.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-457)[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-458) An analysis estimated that Meta, the parent company of Facebook and Instagram, could gain between $2.46 billion and $3.38 billion in advertising revenue if TikTok were banned.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-459)
### Alleged censorship of criticism of Donald Trump and Jeffrey Epstein
In 2026 TikTok was criticized for allegedly censoring criticism of [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") and references to [Jeffrey Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein "Jeffrey Epstein"), with whom Trump had [a long-standing relationship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relationship_of_Donald_Trump_and_Jeffrey_Epstein "Relationship of Donald Trump and Jeffrey Epstein").[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-indyepstein-14)[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-460) California governor [Gavin Newsom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavin_Newsom "Gavin Newsom") said the Government of California was launching an investigation of TikTok for violating California law by censoring Trump-critical content.[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-461)[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-462) TikTok claimed it was not deliberately censoring content and blamed alleged power outages.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-463)
### Alleged censorship of anti-ICE videos
In 2026, it was reported by users that they were unable to make and post videos about ICE. TikTok however spoke up in a statement which identifies a power outage at a US data center as the reason for this.[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-464)
## Restrictions and bans
Main article: [Censorship of TikTok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship_of_TikTok "Censorship of TikTok")
  * , but not enforced
  *   * [Douyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Douyin "Douyin") used instead
  * **Not shown:** Banned on [EU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EU "EU") and [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") devices


### Albania
On 21 December 2024, Albanian Prime Minister [Edi Rama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edi_Rama "Edi Rama") announced that the Albanian government will shut down TikTok in 2025 for at least a year, following a deadly incident in November 2024 in which a teenager fatally stabbed another teen after a dispute that began on the platform.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-465)[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-466)[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-467) On 7 March 2025, the shutdown was officially enacted after the [Albanian Cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_\(Albania\) "Council of Ministers \(Albania\)") cited concerns over the app's role in promoting violence and bullying among children.[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-468)
### Canada
On 6 November 2024, Canada ordered TikTok to shut down its offices and subsidiary company (TikTok Technology Canada, Inc.) in the country due to national security concerns, but access to the app was not banned.[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Milmo-2024-469)[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Government_of_Canada-2024-470) Users will still be able to access the video app and upload content to it.[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Milmo-2024-469)[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Government_of_Canada-2024-470)
### European Union
