In February 2023, the [European Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament"), the [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission"), and the [Council of the European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union "Council of the European Union"), have all banned TikTok on staff devices, citing cybersecurity concerns.[[470]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-471)[[471]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-472)
### India
In 2020, TikTok was banned indefinitely in India after the country had a [border clash with China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_China%E2%80%93India_skirmishes "2020–2021 China–India skirmishes").[[472]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-473)
### United States
Main article: [Restrictions on TikTok in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restrictions_on_TikTok_in_the_United_States "Restrictions on TikTok in the United States")
In January 2020, the United States Army and Navy banned TikTok on government devices after the [Defense Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") labeled it a security risk. Recruiters had been using the app to help fill quotas, and some continue to maintain a level of engagement through their personal accounts.[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-474)[[474]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-475)[[475]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-476)
According to a 2020 article in _The New York Times_ , [Central Intelligence Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") analysts determined that while it is possible the Chinese government could obtain user information from the app, there was no evidence it had done so.[[476]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-477)
#### Federal level
On 6 August 2020, [US President Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "First presidency of Donald Trump") signed an order[[477]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-478)[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-479) which would ban TikTok transactions in 45 days if it was not sold by ByteDance.[[479]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-480)[[480]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Arbel-2020-481) On 14 August 2020, Trump issued another order[[481]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-482) giving ByteDance 90 days to sell or spin off its US TikTok business.[[482]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-483) In the order, Trump said that there is "credible evidence" that leads him to believe that ByteDance "might take action that threatens to impair the national security of the United States".[[483]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-484)
In June 2021, US President [Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") signed an executive order revoking the Trump administration ban on TikTok, and instead ordered the [Secretary of Commerce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary_of_Commerce "Secretary of Commerce") to investigate the app to determine if it poses a threat to US national security.[[484]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-485) On 27 December 2022, the [Chief Administrative Officer of the United States House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Administrative_Officer_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives "Chief Administrative Officer of the United States House of Representatives") banned TikTok from all devices managed by the House of Representatives.[[485]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-486) On 30 December 2022, President Joe Biden signed the [No TikTok on Government Devices Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_TikTok_on_Government_Devices_Act "No TikTok on Government Devices Act"), prohibiting the use of the app on devices owned by the federal government, with some exceptions.[[486]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-487)
On 13 March 2024, the [United States House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives") passed [H.R. 7521](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H.R._7521 "H.R. 7521"), which would ban TikTok entirely unless it was divested from its Chinese parent company, ByteDance.[[487]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-488) In April, the House of Representatives included a revised version of the bill in a foreign aid package, which was passed by the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") on 23 April 2024, and signed into law by President Joe Biden the following day.[[488]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-489)[[489]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-490)[[490]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-491) The law was challenged in [TikTok, Inc. v. Garland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok,_Inc._v._Garland "TikTok, Inc. v. Garland") but was upheld as constitutional. In response to the potential ban, many users signed up for the Chinese app [Xiaohongshu (Chinese: 小红书)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xiaohongshu "Xiaohongshu"), known internationally as REDnote.[[491]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-492) On 18 January 2025, hours before the bill went into effect, TikTok became unavailable across the country.[[492]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-493)[[493]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-494) The next day, TikTok restored access to their service after re-elected [US President Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "Second presidency of Donald Trump") assured TikTok he would not enforce the law.[[494]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-495)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Associated_Press-2025-64) President Trump signed an executive order on 20 January 2025, delaying the enforcement of the TikTok ban by 75 days.[[495]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-496)[[496]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-497) In April 2025, President Trump signed another executive order further delaying the enforcement of the TikTok ban by 75 days,[[497]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-498) and did so again in June 2025 with a 90-day extension.[[498]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-499)
#### State level
As of February 2023, at least 32 (of 50) states have announced or enacted bans on state government agencies, employees, and contractors using TikTok on government-issued devices. State bans only affect government employees and do not prohibit civilians from having or using the app on their personal devices.[[499]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-500)[[500]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-501)
#### Observations
Critics say the United States itself surveils individuals abroad via tech companies under [FISA laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_Intelligence_Surveillance_Act_of_1978_Amendments_Act_of_2008 "Foreign Intelligence Surveillance Act of 1978 Amendments Act of 2008").[[501]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-aj202303282-502) Data collected by TikTok and other social networks can already be purchased through other means.[[501]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-aj202303282-502)[[502]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Chin-2022-503) Some theorize that, if passed, H.R. 7521 could "embolden authoritarian censorship" of American Internet companies and affect US interests, reputation, and online speech.[[503]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-504) They have also labeled a potential ban on the app an assault on [freedom of speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech"), including Republican congressmen [Rand Paul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rand_Paul "Rand Paul") and [Thomas Massie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Massie "Thomas Massie").[[504]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-505)[[505]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-506)
Observers have argued that the national security concerns raised are largely hypothetical.[[506]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-507)[[507]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-CNN20240312-508)[[508]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-conversation-509) There is insufficient public evidence to show that American user data has been accessed by or shared with the PRC government,[[509]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-510)[[510]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Chicago_Policy_Review_7-26-2023-511)[[511]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-CNN_Business_3-21-2023-512) with some claims reportedly exaggerated.[[512]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-atlantic-513) Biden himself was on TikTok as the president, while Trump has reversed his previous position.[[513]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-514) According to computer security specialist [Bruce Schneier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruce_Schneier "Bruce Schneier"), which company owns TikTok may not matter, as [Russia had interfered in the 2016 US elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_interference_in_the_2016_United_States_elections "Russian interference in the 2016 United States elections") using [Facebook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook#Russian_interference "Facebook") without owning it.[[514]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-Intercept2024-515)
## Partnerships
In April 2021, the [Abu Dhabi Department of Culture and Tourism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Department_of_Culture_and_Tourism "Abu Dhabi Department of Culture and Tourism") partnered with TikTok to promote tourism for the [city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Dhabi "Abu Dhabi").[[515]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-516) It came following the January 2021 winter campaign with the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates") Government Media Office.[[516]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-517)
In June 2023, _[The New Zealand Herald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_Zealand_Herald "The New Zealand Herald")_ reported that TikTok, working in cooperation with both New Zealand and Australian police, deleted 340 accounts and 2,000 videos associated with criminal gangs including the [Mongrel Mob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongrel_Mob "Mongrel Mob"), [Black Power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Power_\(New_Zealand_gang\) "Black Power \(New Zealand gang\)"), [Killer Beez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killer_Beez "Killer Beez"), the [Comancheros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comanchero_Motorcycle_Club "Comanchero Motorcycle Club"), [Mongols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongols_Motorcycle_Club "Mongols Motorcycle Club"), and [Rebels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebels_Motorcycle_Club "Rebels Motorcycle Club"). TikTok had earlier drawn criticism for hosting content by organized crime groups promoting the gang lifestyle and fights. A TikTok spokesperson reiterated the platform's efforts to countering "violent" and "hateful" organizations' content and cooperating with police. [New Zealand Police Commissioner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand_Police_Commissioner "New Zealand Police Commissioner") [Andrew Coster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Coster "Andrew Coster") praised the platform for taking a "socially-responsible stance" against gangs.[[517]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-518)
TikTok has partnered with the [Hispanic Heritage Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic_Heritage_Foundation "Hispanic Heritage Foundation") to support small [Latino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans "Hispanic and Latino Americans") businesses, setting aside $5000 each for 40 grant recipients based on [entrepreneurship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entrepreneurship "Entrepreneurship").[[518]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-519) After digital advertising rules for the Olympics were relaxed, TikTok and [Team GB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Team_GB "Team GB") signed a sponsorship deal to help UK athletes connect with new audiences for the [2024 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Summer_Olympics "2024 Summer Olympics").[[519]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-520)
Starting in 2021, TikTok became the primary sponsor/partner of the [English Football League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Football_League "English Football League") club [Wrexham A.F.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C. "Wrexham A.F.C.") located in [Wrexham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrexham "Wrexham"), Wales. A large version of the TikTok logo was emblazoned on the front of the player's red coloured home and away uniforms below the Wrexham A.F.C. crest as well as on shirts sold by Wrexham's brick and mortar and virtual fan stores, the partnership ended in 2023 when Wrexham was promoted to the [EFL League Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EFL_League_Two "EFL League Two") after which US airline [United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Airlines "United Airlines") took over the partnership/sponsorship.[[520]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-521)[[521]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-522)
On 8 January 2026, TikTok announced a new partnership with the FIFA World Cup.[[522]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-523)
In early 2026, the United States and China approved a deal transferring operational control of TikTok's US business to a joint venture led by Oracle and Silver Lake, following a 2024 US law requiring ByteDance to divest the platform over national security concerns.[[523]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-524) [Shou Chew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shou_Chew "Shou Chew") announced in a memo addressed to employees that TikTok will henceforth operate in the United States under a joint investment entity in which the majority ownership will be American.[[524]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-525)[[525]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-526) Under the agreement reached, it is guaranteed that Americans will be protected on the social network TikTok through “data protection,” “content oversight,” and “algorithm security.”[[526]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-527)[[527]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-528)[[528]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok#cite_note-529)

Furthermore, U.S. private companies, such as Clearview AI, Palantir, and Giant Oak have collectively scanned billions of social media posts—which could include TikTok content."
